                <br /><hr />
                <strong> What is Performances Testing?</strong><br />
                    <span style=" font-size:14px;">
                        What is Load Testing?
                        Load Testing is a process to design and simulate usage traffic which can be used to test your server for performance, reliability and scalability. Load Testing of websites involves testing the performance and scalability of your web servers with varying user load. Load testing involves simulating real-life user load for the target website. It helps you determine how your website behaves when multiple users hits it simultaneously. Load testing with different load strategies and conditions helps you determine software design issues like incorrect concurrency/pooling mechanism, poor optimization, memory build-up, etc. Load Testing helps you identify server configuration issues with Web server, application server, database server, load balancer, etc. Load Testing helps you detect if your current infrastructure is sufficient to meet your user demand. Load Testing helps you determine the peak user load your website can sustain, number of concurrent users your website can support, and whether or not your website will scale as more users access it.
                       
                        <script async src="//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js"></script>
                        <!-- H_Page -->
                        <ins class="adsbygoogle"
                             style="display:inline-block;width:728px;height:90px"
                             data-ad-client="ca-pub-2242131967064788"
                             data-ad-slot="2118144356"></ins>
                        <script>
                            (adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});
                        </script>
                         <br />
                        <strong> Load testing will provide you answers of below questions:</strong>
                        <br />
                        â¢	Do you know the number of concurrent users that your website can safely support?
                    <br />
                    â¢	Will your website scale as more users access it?
                    <br />
                    â¢	Do you know how long it would take a visitor to receive a page?
                    <br />
                    â¢	Do you know the load point where your server crashes?
                    <br />
                    â¢	Is your current hardware sufficient to meet your predicted demand? If no, what additional hardware would you need?
Load Testing can help you identify a variety of problems before you go into production:
                    <br />
                    â¢	Software design issues (incorrect concurrency/pooling mechanism, poor optimization, memory build-up, etc.)
                    <br />
                    â¢	Server configuration issues (Web server, application server, database server, load balancer, etc.)
                    <br />
                    â¢	Hardware limitation issues (Excessive disk I/O, CPU maximization, memory limitations, network bottleneck, etc.)


                    
                    </span>

    <div style=" margin:10px; font-family:Verdana">
    <div id="head_divStart" style="margin-left: 40px">
         <strong>What is Correlation in Load Runner?
        </strong><br /><br />
        Correlation is used to obtain data which are unique for each run of the script and which are generated by web server. Correlation provides the value to avoid errors arising out of duplicate values and also optimizing the code. Automatic correlation is where we set some rules for correlation. It can be application server specific. Here values are replaced by data which are created by these rules. In manual correlation, the value we want to correlate is scanned and create correlation is used to correlate.
        <br /><br />
        <strong>Correlation Challenge- Modrate</strong><br />
    
        <br />
        Welcome to the Correlation Challenge. I have condensed some of the types of 
        correlation problems I have encountered in real web applications (ranging from 
        relatively easy, to fairly difficult) into this exercise. You should be able to 
        manually navigate through the Challenge with no problems, but creating a 
        LoadRunner/VuGen script that will do the same thing will take a non-trivial 
        amount of effort. Please treat this as a training exercise. If you can get to 
        the end of this exercise by yourself, then you can correlate with the best of 
        them.<br />
        <br />
        <strong>Notes</strong>:
        <br />
        â¢ The Challenges must be attempted in the order given.
        <br />
        â¢ You must have JavaScript enabled in your browser to proceed through this 
        challenge manually.
        <br />
        â¢ Please donât share your solutions, ask for help, or help others. This is meant 
        to be a challenge.
        <br />
        â¢ Please email me if you find any bugs that are not obviously part of the 
        challenge (deepak at loadrunnertips.com)
        <br />
        â¢ If you email me your (zipped) solution, I will list your name/website/company 
        here.<br />
    
        <br />
